9:[["$","meta","0",{"name":"viewport","content":"width=device-width, initial-scale=1"}],["$","meta","1",{"charSet":"utf-8"}],["$","title","2",{"children":"D10f | Automated Docker Swarm Lab Environment"}],["$","meta","3",{"name":"description","content":"Create a multi-node lab environment locally or on a remote server running as a Docker Swarm."}],["$","meta","4",{"name":"keywords","content":"linux, docker, vagrant, ansible, docker,ansible,vagrant"}]]
1:null
a:I[3475,["750","static/chunks/750-0f816d740819c251.js","308","static/chunks/app/blog/%5Bslug%5D/page-920a7887c59b1504.js"],"default"]
b:T46379,<div id="preamble">
<div class="sectionbody">
<div class="paragraph">
<p>Having a throw-away environment is essential to experiment with new technologies, new features and run tests before deploying to production. Tools like Vagrant allow you to manage entire fleets of virtual machines through a convenient configuration file written in a friendly-yet-powerful programming language.</p>
</div>
</div>
</div><menu class="toc"><li class="toc__item"><a href="#_objective">Objective</a></li><li class="toc__item"><a href="#_defining_the_infrastructure">Defining The Infrastructure</a></li><li class="toc__item"><a href="#_configuring_the_virtual_machines">Configuring The Virtual Machines</a><ul><li class="toc__item"><a href="#_ansible_playbook">Ansible Playbook</a></li><li class="toc__item"><a href="#_docker_role">Docker Role</a></li><li class="toc__item"><a href="#_docker_swarm_role">Docker Swarm Role</a></li></ul></li></menu>
<div class="sect1"><h2 id="_objective">Objective<a class="anchor" href="#_objective">
                    <svg aria-hidden="true">
                        <use href="/sprite.svg#icon-link" />
                    </svg>
                </a></h2>
<div class="sectionbody">
<div class="paragraph">
<p>This post covers how to create a simple setup of 3 virtual machines running as a Docker Swarm. A Vagrantfile will be used to configure things like the operating system and RAM for each host, while Ansible will handle all the configuration inside the machine at the application layer &mdash; things like installed software, users, permissions, firewall rules, etc.</p>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="sect1"><h2 id="_defining_the_infrastructure">Defining The Infrastructure<a class="anchor" href="#_defining_the_infrastructure">
                    <svg aria-hidden="true">
                        <use href="/sprite.svg#icon-link" />
                    </svg>
                </a></h2>
<div class="sectionbody">
<div class="paragraph">
<p>A <code>Vagrantfile</code> is the starting point where everything pertaining to the infrastructure will be defined. This includes the number of virtual machines, how much memory each virtual machine will have, the operating system, network interfaces, etc. It can be as simple or as complex as needed.</p>
</div>

            <td>
                <i class="conum pr-2" data-value="1"></i>
                <b>❶</b>
            </td>
            <td>When all machines are created, we can provision them.</td>
        </tr><tr>
            <td>
                <i class="conum pr-2" data-value="2"></i>
                <b>❷</b>
            </td>
            <td>The provisioner can be a shell script, but Ansible is a much more powerful tool for this.</td>
        </tr><tr>
            <td>
                <i class="conum pr-2" data-value="3"></i>
                <b>❸</b>
            </td>
            <td>Set the limit to "all" to allow the provisioner to run in parallel.</td>
        </tr><tr>
            <td>
                <i class="conum pr-2" data-value="4"></i>
                <b>❹</b>
            </td>
            <td>The path to the Ansible playbook that will run for each machine.</td>

            </div>
        </div>
<div class="colist arabic">
                <table>
                    <tbody>
                        <tr>
            <td>
                <i class="conum pr-2" data-value="1"></i>
                <b>❶</b>
            </td>
            <td>Create variables for each host that Ansible will use.</td>
        </tr><tr>
            <td>
                <i class="conum pr-2" data-value="2"></i>
                <b>❷</b>
            </td>
            <td>Define groups of hosts for Ansible to determine when to run.</td>
        </tr>
                    </tbody>
                </table>
            </div>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>This last step can be simplified quite a bit, and you probably want to do so in the event that you have more than just a few machines, otherwise entering these details manually becomes cumbersome really quick. But for the purposes of this post, this makes things clearer (I hope).</p>
</div>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>This Vagrantfile will create 3 virtual machines running Debian 12 Bookworm and 1 GB of RAM. Ansible understands this setup to be comprised of two "workers" and one "manager", which will be used later in the playbook to determine which actions to run on each host.</p>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="sect1"><h2 id="_configuring_the_virtual_machines">Configuring The Virtual Machines<a class="anchor" href="#_configuring_the_virtual_machines">
                    <svg aria-hidden="true">
                        <use href="/sprite.svg#icon-link" />
                    </svg>
                </a></h2>
<div class="sectionbody">
<div class="paragraph">
<p>In order to configure each machine we are going to write an Ansible playbook, as specified in the Vagrantfile.</p>
</div>
<div class="sect2"><h3 id="_ansible_playbook">Ansible Playbook<a class="anchor" href="#_ansible_playbook">
                    <svg aria-hidden="true">
                        <use href="/sprite.svg#icon-link" />
                    </svg>
                </a></h3>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>This playbook assumes the existence of two roles: docker and docker-swarm, each containing the respective tasks to configure the host in the exact same way. There more ways to do this but for simplicity only the essentials are described in this post.</p>
</div>

<div class="sect2"><h3 id="_docker_role">Docker Role<a class="anchor" href="#_docker_role">
                    <svg aria-hidden="true">
                        <use href="/sprite.svg#icon-link" />
                    </svg>
                </a></h3>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>We could break things down to make this playbook much more modular so that it works with other Linux distributions, or in case things like dependencies change in the future. For simplicity though, it&#8217;s aimed to work with Debian specifically.</p>
</div>
<div class="codeblock">

                </figure>
            </div>
        </div>
<div class="colist arabic">
                <table>
                    <tbody>
                        <tr>
            <td>
                <i class="conum pr-2" data-value="1"></i>
                <b>❶</b>
            </td>
            <td>The deb822 format is the new standard in Debian and derivative distributions, even though it's not reflected in Docker's documentation which still uses the previous format.</td>
        </tr><tr>

                <b>❷</b>

        </tr><tr>
            <td>
                <i class="conum pr-2" data-value="3"></i>
                <b>❸</b>

</div>
<div class="sect2"><h3 id="_docker_swarm_role">Docker Swarm Role<a class="anchor" href="#_docker_swarm_role">
                    <svg aria-hidden="true">
                        <use href="/sprite.svg#icon-link" />
                    </svg>
                </a></h3>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>This role initializes the Docker Swarm and then instructs all hosts to join in. Remember how in the <code>Vagrantfile</code> we used the <code>ansible.limit = "all"</code> option? This was used to parallelize the work so that the playbook runs on all hosts at once, which naturally creates a race condition in this case: how does a worker node to join the swarm if it hasn&#8217;t been created yet? Specifying a timeout for this task is important as it will re-try to join until it succeeds.</p>
</div>
<div class="paragraph">
<p>It would be safer to run the playbook for each host in sequence as they are created. However, this causes another problem that is not that easy to work around: the Ansible instance running on each node does so in isolation and cannot figure out the necessary credentials to join the swarm.</p>
</div>

            <button class="codeblock__copy-btn rotating-btn mt-6 js-required">
                <span class="unselectable">
                    <svg aria-hidden="true">
                        <use href="/sprite.svg#icon-clipboard" />
                    </svg>

                    <svg aria-hidden="true" style="transform: rotate(180deg);">
                        <use href="/sprite.svg#icon-clipboard-success" />
                    </svg>
                </span>
            </button>
